</section><section data-mw-section-id="11" id="mwAgE"><h3 id="Plantation_cultivation">Plantation cultivation</h3> 

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt279" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"further","href":"./Template:Further"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"History of modern banana plantations in the Americas"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAgI"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt279" id="mwAgM">Further information: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./History_of_modern_banana_plantations_in_the_Americas" title="History of modern banana plantations in the Americas">History of modern banana plantations in the Americas</a></div>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAgQ"><a href="./File:Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAgU"><img resource="./File:Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg/220px-Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" data-file-type="bitmap" height="165" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg/330px-Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg/440px-Banana_Plantation_Panabo_City.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwAgY"/></a><figcaption id="mwAgc">Plantation in the Philippines, 2010</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwAgg">In the 15th and 16th centuries, Portuguese colonists started banana plantations in the Atlantic Islands, Brazil, and western Africa.<sup about="#mwt285" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Phora_52-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Phora"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Phora-52" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 52;" id="mwAgk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAgo">[52]</span></a></sup> North Americans began consuming bananas on a small scale at very high prices shortly after the Civil War, though it was only in the 1880s that the food became more widespread.<sup about="#mwt286" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Koep08_53-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Koep08"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Koep08-53" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 53;" id="mwAgs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAgw">[53]</span></a></sup> As late as the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Victorian_Era" title="Victorian Era" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAg0">Victorian Era</a>, bananas were not widely known in Europe, although they were available.<sup about="#mwt287" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Phora_52-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Phora"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Phora-52" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 52;" id="mwAg4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAg8">[52]</span></a></sup> 
The earliest modern plantations originated in Jamaica and the related <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Western_Caribbean_Zone" title="Western Caribbean Zone" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAhA">Western Caribbean Zone</a>, including most of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Central_America" title="Central America" id="mwAhE">Central America</a>. It involved the combination of modern transportation networks of steamships and railroads with the development of refrigeration that allowed more time between harvesting and ripening. North American shippers like <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lorenzo_Dow_Baker" title="Lorenzo Dow Baker" id="mwAhI">Lorenzo Dow Baker</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Andrew_Preston_(businessman)" title="Andrew Preston (businessman)" id="mwAhM">Andrew Preston</a>, the founders of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Boston_Fruit_Company" title="Boston Fruit Company" id="mwAhQ">Boston Fruit Company</a> started this process in the 1870s, but railroad builders like <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Minor_C._Keith" title="Minor C. Keith" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAhU">Minor C. Keith</a> participated, culminating in the multi-national giant corporations like <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chiquita_Brands_International" title="Chiquita Brands International" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAhY">Chiquita</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dole_Food_Company" title="Dole Food Company" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAhc">Dole</a>.<sup about="#mwt291" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Koep08_53-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Koep08"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Koep08-53" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 53;" id="mwAhg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAhk">[53]</span></a></sup> These companies were <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Monopoly" title="Monopoly" id="mwAho">monopolistic</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vertically_integrated" title="Vertically integrated" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAhs">vertically integrated</a> (controlling growing, processing, shipping and marketing) and usually used political manipulation to build <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Enclave_economy" title="Enclave economy" id="mwAhw">enclave economies</a> (internally self-sufficient, virtually tax exempt, and export-oriented, contributing little to the host economy). Their political maneuvers, which gave rise to the term <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_republic" title="Banana republic" id="mwAh0">banana republic</a> for states such as Honduras and Guatemala, included working with local elites and their rivalries to influence politics or playing the international interests of the United States, especially during the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cold_War" title="Cold War" id="mwAh4">Cold War</a>, to keep the political climate favorable to their interests.<sup about="#mwt292" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-NZH_54-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"NZH"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-NZH-54" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 54;" id="mwAh8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAiA">[54]</span></a></sup> In the modern United States, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hawaii" title="Hawaii" id="mwAiE">Hawaii</a> is by far the largest banana producer, followed by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Florida" title="Florida" id="mwAiI">Florida</a>.<sup about="#mwt296" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-55" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-55"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-55" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 55;" id="mwAiM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAiQ">[55]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="12" id="mwAiU"><h3 id="Peasant_cultivation">Peasant cultivation</h3>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAiY"><a href="./File:Farm_Workers.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAic"><img resource="./File:Farm_Workers.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Farm_Workers.jpg/220px-Farm_Workers.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1696" data-file-height="954" data-file-type="bitmap" height="124" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Farm_Workers.jpg/330px-Farm_Workers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Farm_Workers.jpg/440px-Farm_Workers.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwAig"/></a><figcaption id="mwAik">Small-scale banana production, Liberia, 2013</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwAio">The vast majority of the world's bananas are cultivated for family consumption or for sale on local markets. India is the world leader in this sort of production, but many other Asian and African countries where climate and soil conditions allow cultivation also host large populations of banana growers who sell at least some of their crop.<sup about="#mwt298" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOffice_of_the_Gene_Technology_Regulator20087–8_56-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Office of the Gene Technology Regulator"},"2":{"wt":"2008"},"pp":{"wt":"7–8"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOffice_of_the_Gene_Technology_Regulator20087–8-56" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 56;" id="mwAis"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAiw">[56]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./History_of_peasant_banana_production_in_the_Americas" title="History of peasant banana production in the Americas" id="mwAi0">Peasants with smallholdings of 1 to 2 acres in the Caribbean produce bananas</a> for the world market, often alongside other crops.<sup about="#mwt301" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-57" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-57"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-57" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 57;" id="mwAi4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAi8">[57]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="13" id="mwAjA"><h2 id="Modern_cultivation">Modern cultivation</h2>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt302" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"see also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"List of banana cultivars"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAjE"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt302" id="mwAjI">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_banana_cultivars" title="List of banana cultivars">List of banana cultivars</a></div>

<p id="mwAjM">Bananas are propagated <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Asexual_reproduction" title="Asexual reproduction" id="mwAjQ">asexually</a> from offshoots. The plant is allowed to produce two shoots at a time; a larger one for immediate fruiting and a smaller "sucker" or "follower" to produce fruit in 6–8 months.<sup about="#mwt307" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStoverSimmonds1987244–247_8-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Stover"},"2":{"wt":"Simmonds"},"3":{"wt":"1987"},"pp":{"wt":"244–247"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStoverSimmonds1987244–247-8" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 8;" id="mwAjU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAjY">[8]</span></a></sup> As a non-seasonal crop, bananas are available fresh year-round.<sup about="#mwt313" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-58" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-58"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-58" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 58;" id="mwAjc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAjg">[58]</span></a></sup> They are grown in some 135 countries.<sup about="#mwt317" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-59" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-59"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-59" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 59;" id="mwAjk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAjo">[59]</span></a></sup></p>

<section data-mw-section-id="14" id="mwAjs"><h3 id="Cavendish">Cavendish</h3>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt318" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Cavendish banana"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAjw"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt318" id="mwAj0">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cavendish_banana" title="Cavendish banana">Cavendish banana</a></div>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAj4"><a href="./File:Bananas.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAj8"><img alt="Grocery store photo of several bunches of bananas" resource="./File:Bananas.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bananas.jpg/220px-Bananas.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" data-file-type="bitmap" height="146" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bananas.jpg/330px-Bananas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bananas.jpg/440px-Bananas.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwAkA"/></a><figcaption id="mwAkE">Cultivars in the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cavendish_bananas" title="Cavendish bananas" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAkI">Cavendish</a> group dominate the world market.</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwAkM">In global commerce in 2009, by far the most important cultivars belonged to the triploid <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_banana_cultivars#AAA_Group" title="List of banana cultivars" id="mwAkQ">AAA group</a> of Cavendish group bananas.<sup about="#mwt326" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-60" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-60"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-60" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 60;" id="mwAkU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAkY">[60]</span></a></sup> It is unclear if any existing cultivar can replace Cavendish bananas, so various <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)" id="mwAkc">hybridisation</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering" id="mwAkg">genetic engineering</a> programs are attempting to create a disease-resistant, mass-market banana. One such strain that has emerged is the Taiwanese Cavendish or Formosana.<sup about="#mwt330" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Gittleson_2018_61-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Gittleson 2018"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Gittleson_2018-61"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Gittleson_2018-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAkk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAko">[61]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="15" id="mwAks"><h3 id="Ripening">Ripening</h3>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAkw"><a href="./File:Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAk0"><img resource="./File:Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg/220px-Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="5344" data-file-height="2832" data-file-type="bitmap" height="117" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg/330px-Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg/440px-Overripe_banana_20211221_152406.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwAk4"/></a><figcaption id="mwAk8"><i id="mwAlA"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ralstonia_solanacearum" title="Ralstonia solanacearum" id="mwAlE">Ralstonia solanacearum</a></i> on an overripe banana</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwAlI">Export bananas are picked green, and ripened in special rooms upon arrival in the destination country. These rooms are air-tight and filled with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ethylene_as_a_plant_hormone" title="Ethylene as a plant hormone" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAlM">ethylene gas</a> to induce ripening. This mimics the normal production of this gas as a ripening hormone.<sup about="#mwt338" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-plantphys_62-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"plantphys"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-plantphys-62" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 62;" id="mwAlQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAlU">[62]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt339" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-newton_63-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"newton"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-newton-63" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 63;" id="mwAlY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAlc">[63]</span></a></sup> Ethylene stimulates the formation of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amylase" title="Amylase" id="mwAlg">amylase</a>, an <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Enzyme" title="Enzyme" id="mwAlk">enzyme</a> that breaks down starch into sugar, influencing the taste. Ethylene signals the production of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pectinase" title="Pectinase" id="mwAlo">pectinase</a>, an <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Enzyme" title="Enzyme" id="mwAls">enzyme</a> which breaks down the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pectin" title="Pectin" id="mwAlw">pectin</a> between the cells of the banana, causing the banana to soften as it ripens.<sup about="#mwt340" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-plantphys_62-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"plantphys"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-plantphys-62" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 62;" id="mwAl0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAl4">[62]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt341" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-newton_63-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"newton"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-newton-63" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 63;" id="mwAl8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmA">[63]</span></a></sup> The vivid yellow color consumers normally associate with supermarket bananas is caused by ripening around <span about="#mwt336" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"18"},"2":{"wt":"C"},"3":{"wt":"F"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAmE">18</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt336"> </span><span about="#mwt336">°C (64</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt336"> </span><span about="#mwt336">°F)</span>, and does not occur in Cavendish bananas ripened in tropical temperatures (over <span about="#mwt337" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"27"},"2":{"wt":"C"},"3":{"wt":"F"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAmI">27</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt337"> </span><span about="#mwt337">°C (81</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt337"> </span><span about="#mwt337">°F)</span>).<sup about="#mwt342" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Ding07_64-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Ding07"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Ding07-64" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 64;" id="mwAmM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmQ">[64]</span></a></sup></p> 

</section><section data-mw-section-id="16" id="mwAmU"><h3 id="Storage_and_transport">Storage and transport</h3>

<p id="mwAmY">Bananas are transported over long distances from the tropics to world markets.<sup about="#mwt350" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FAO-2003_65-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"FAO-2003"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-FAO-2003-65"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-FAO-2003-65" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 65;" id="mwAmc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmg">[65]</span></a></sup> To obtain maximum shelf life, harvest comes before the fruit is mature. The fruit requires careful handling, rapid transport to ports, cooling, and refrigerated shipping. The goal is to prevent the bananas from producing their natural ripening agent, ethylene. This technology allows storage and transport for 3–4 weeks at <span about="#mwt345" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"13"},"2":{"wt":"C"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAmk">13</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt345"> </span><span about="#mwt345">°C (55</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt345"> </span><span about="#mwt345">°F)</span>. On arrival, bananas are held at about <span about="#mwt346" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"17"},"2":{"wt":"C"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAmo">17</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt346"> </span><span about="#mwt346">°C (63</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt346"> </span><span about="#mwt346">°F)</span> and treated with a low concentration of ethylene. After a few days, the fruit begins to ripen and is distributed for final sale. Ripe bananas can be held for a few days at home. If bananas are too green, they can be put in a brown paper bag with an apple or tomato overnight to speed up the ripening process.<sup about="#mwt351" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ChiquitaRipen_66-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ChiquitaRipen"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-ChiquitaRipen-66" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 66;" id="mwAms"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAmw">[66]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="17" id="mwAm0"><h3 id="Sustainability">Sustainability</h3>

<p id="mwAm4">The excessive use of fertilizers contributes greatly to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication" id="mwAm8">eutrophication</a> in streams and lakes, and harms aquatic life after algal blooms deprive fish of oxygen. It has been theorized that destruction of 60% of coral reefs along the coasts of Costa Rica is partially from sediments from banana plantations. Another issue is the deforestation associated with expanding banana production. As monocultures rapidly deplete soil nutrients plantations expand to areas with rich soils and cut down forests, which also affects soil erosion and degradation, and increases frequency of flooding. The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAnA">World Wildlife Fund</a> stated that banana production produced more waste than any other agricultural sector, with discarded banana plants, bags used to cover the bananas, strings to tie them, and containers for transport.<sup about="#mwt356" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen2009_67-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Cohen2009"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Cohen2009-67"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Cohen2009-67" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 67;" id="mwAnE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAnI">[67]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAnM"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sustainability_standards_and_certification" title="Sustainability standards and certification" id="mwAnQ">Voluntary sustainability standards</a> such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rainforest_Alliance" title="Rainforest Alliance" id="mwAnU">Rainforest Alliance</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fairtrade_certification" title="Fairtrade certification" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAnY">Fairtrade</a> are being used to address some of these issues. Bananas production certified in this way grew rapidly at the start of the 21st century to represent 36% of banana exports by 2016.<sup about="#mwt361" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-68" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-68"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-68" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 68;" id="mwAnc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAng">[68]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="18" id="mwAnk"><h2 id="Breeding">Breeding</h2>

<p id="mwAno"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mutation_breeding" title="Mutation breeding" id="mwAns">Mutation breeding</a> can be used in this crop. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aneuploidy" title="Aneuploidy" id="mwAnw">Aneuploidy</a> is a source of significant variation in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Allotriploid" title="Allotriploid" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAn0">allotriploid</a> varieties. For one example, it can be a source of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Panama_disease#Tropical_Race_4/TR4" title="Panama disease" id="mwAn4">TR4 resistance</a>. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lab_protocol" title="Lab protocol" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAn8">Lab protocols</a> have been devised to screen for such aberrations and for possible resulting disease resistances.<sup about="#mwt367" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Efficient-Screening-Mutants_69-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Efficient-Screening-Mutants"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Efficient-Screening-Mutants-69"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Efficient-Screening-Mutants-69" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 69;" id="mwAoA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAoE">[69]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crop_wild_relative" title="Crop wild relative" id="mwAoI">Wild <i id="mwAoM">Musa</i> spp.</a> provide useful resistance genetics, and are vital to breeding for TR4 resistance, as shown in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Introgressed" title="Introgressed" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAoQ">introgressed</a> resistance from wild relatives.<sup about="#mwt371" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Current-Update_70-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Current-Update"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Current-Update-70"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Current-Update-70" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 70;" id="mwAoU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAoY">[70]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwAoc">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Honduran_Foundation_for_Agricultural_Research" title="Honduran Foundation for Agricultural Research" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAog">Honduran Foundation for Agricultural Research</a> attempted to exploit the rare cases of seed production to create disease-resistant varieties by conventional breeding; 30,000 commercial banana plants were hand-pollinated with pollen from wild fertile Asian fruit, producing 400 tonnes, which contained about fifteen seeds, of which four or five germinated. Further breeding with wild bananas yielded a new seedless variety resistant to both black Sigatoka and Panama disease.<sup about="#mwt376" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-71" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-71"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-71" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 71;" id="mwAok"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAoo">[71]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="19" id="mwAos"><h2 id="Production_and_export">Production and export</h2>

<section data-mw-section-id="20" id="mwAow"><h3 id="World">World</h3>

<table class="wikitable floatright" style="width:24em; margin-left: 1em;" id="mwAo0">
<caption id="mwAo4">2022 production (in millions of tonnes)</caption>
<tbody id="mwAo8"><tr id="mwApA">
<th style="background:#ddf; width:70%;" id="mwApE"></th>
<th style="background:#ddf; width:10%;" id="mwApI">Bananas</th>
<th style="background:#ddf; width:10%;" id="mwApM">Plantains</th>

<td id="mwAw0"><span class="flagicon" about="#mwt396" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Flagu","href":"./Template:Flagu"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Dominican Republic"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAw4"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" resource="./File:Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg.png" decoding="async" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" data-file-type="drawing" height="15" width="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Dominican_Republic.svg.png 2x" class="mw-file-element"/></span></span><span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span></span><span about="#mwt396">Dominican Republic</span></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAw8">1.4</td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAxA">1.2</td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAxE">2.5</td></tr>

<td id="mwAxM"><span class="flagicon" about="#mwt397" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Flagu","href":"./Template:Flagu"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Vietnam"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAxQ"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" resource="./File:Flag_of_Vietnam.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/23px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png" decoding="async" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" data-file-type="drawing" height="15" width="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/35px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/45px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png 2x" class="mw-file-element"/></span></span><span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span></span><span about="#mwt397">Vietnam</span></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAxU">2.5</td><td id="mwAxY"></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAxc">2.5</td></tr>
<tr id="mwAxg">
<td id="mwAxk"><span class="flagicon" about="#mwt398" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Flagu","href":"./Template:Flagu"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Peru"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAxo"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" resource="./File:Flag_of_Peru.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/23px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png" decoding="async" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" data-file-type="drawing" height="15" width="23" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/35px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Peru.svg/45px-Flag_of_Peru.svg.png 2x" class="mw-file-element"/></span></span><span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span></span><span about="#mwt398">Peru</span></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAxs">2.4</td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAxw"></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAx0">2.4</td></tr>
<tr id="mwAx4">
<td style="text-align: center;" id="mwAx8"><b id="mwAyA">World</b></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAyE"><b id="mwAyI">135.1</b></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAyM"><b id="mwAyQ">44.2</b></td><td style="text-align:center;" id="mwAyU"><b id="mwAyY">179.3</b></td></tr>
<tr id="mwAyc">
<td colspan="4" id="mwAyg"><small id="mwAyk">Source: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./FAOSTAT" title="FAOSTAT" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAyo">FAOSTAT</a> of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./United_Nations" title="United Nations" id="mwAys">United Nations</a><sup about="#mwt403" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FAOSTAT2022_72-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"FAOSTAT2022"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-FAOSTAT2022-72"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-FAOSTAT2022-72" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 72;" id="mwAyw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAy0">[72]</span></a></sup> Note: Some countries distinguish between bananas and plantains, but four of the top six producers do not, thus necessitating comparisons using the total for bananas and plantains combined.</small></td></tr>
</tbody></table>

<p id="mwAy4">Bananas are exported in larger volume and to a larger value than any other fruit.<sup about="#mwt408" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Gittleson_2018_61-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Gittleson 2018"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Gittleson_2018-61" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;" id="mwAy8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzA">[61]</span></a></sup> In 2022, world production of bananas and plantains combined was 179 million tonnes, led by India and China with a combined total of 26% of global production. Other major producers were Uganda, Indonesia, the Philippines, Nigeria and Ecuador.<sup about="#mwt409" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FAOSTAT2022_72-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"FAOSTAT2022"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-FAOSTAT2022-72" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 72;" id="mwAzE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzI">[72]</span></a></sup> As reported for 2013, total world exports were 20 million tonnes of bananas and 859,000 tonnes of plantains.<sup about="#mwt413" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-faostat13exp_73-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"faostat13exp"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-faostat13exp-73"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-faostat13exp-73" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 73;" id="mwAzM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzQ">[73]</span></a></sup> Ecuador and the Philippines were the leading exporters with 5.4 and 3.3 million tonnes, respectively, and the Dominican Republic was the leading exporter of plantains with 210,350 tonnes.<sup about="#mwt414" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-faostat13exp_73-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"faostat13exp"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-faostat13exp-73" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 73;" id="mwAzU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAzY">[73]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="21" id="mwAzc"><h3 id="Developing_countries">Developing countries</h3>

<p id="mwAzg">Bananas and plantains are a major staple <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Agriculture" title="Agriculture" id="mwAzk">food crop</a> for millions of people in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Developing_country" title="Developing country" id="mwAzo">developing countries</a>. In many tropical countries, the main cultivars produce green (unripe) bananas used for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cooking" title="Cooking" id="mwAzs">cooking</a>. Most producers are small-scale <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Farmer" title="Farmer" id="mwAzw">farmers</a> either for home consumption or local markets. Because bananas and plantains produce fruit year-round, they provide a valuable food source during the <i id="mwAz0">hunger season</i> between harvests of other crops. Bananas and plantains are thus important for global <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Food_security" title="Food security" id="mwAz4">food security</a>.<sup about="#mwt419" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-dhon_74-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"dhon"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-dhon-74"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-dhon-74" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 74;" id="mwAz8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA0A">[74]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="22" id="mwA0E"><h2 id="Pests">Pests</h2>

<section data-mw-section-id="23" id="mwA0I"><h3 id="Nematodes">Nematodes</h3>

<p id="mwA0M">Banana roots are subject to damage from multiple species of parasitic <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nematode" title="Nematode" id="mwA0Q">nematodes</a>. <i id="mwA0U"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Radopholus_similis" title="Radopholus similis" id="mwA0Y">Radopholus similis</a></i> causes nematode root rot, the most serious nematode disease of bananas in economic terms.<sup about="#mwt424" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sekora_Crow_2012_75-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sekora Crow 2012"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Sekora_Crow_2012-75"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Sekora_Crow_2012-75" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 75;" id="mwA0c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA0g">[75]</span></a></sup> Root-knot is the result of infection by species of <i id="mwA0k"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Meloidogyne" title="Meloidogyne" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA0o">Meloidogyne</a></i>,<sup about="#mwt428" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-76" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-76"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-76" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 76;" id="mwA0s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA0w">[76]</span></a></sup> while root-lesion is caused by species of <i id="mwA00"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pratylenchus" title="Pratylenchus" id="mwA04">Pratylenchus</a></i>,<sup about="#mwt432" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Nyang’au_Atandi_Cortada_Nchore_2021_77-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Nyang’au Atandi Cortada Nchore 2021"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Nyang’au_Atandi_Cortada_Nchore_2021-77"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Nyang’au_Atandi_Cortada_Nchore_2021-77" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 77;" id="mwA08"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA1A">[77]</span></a></sup> and spiral nematode root damage is the result of infection by <i id="mwA1E"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Helicotylenchus" title="Helicotylenchus" id="mwA1I">Helicotylenchus</a></i> species.<sup about="#mwt436" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Zuckerman_1963_78-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Zuckerman 1963"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Zuckerman_1963-78"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Zuckerman_1963-78" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 78;" id="mwA1M"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA1Q">[78]</span></a></sup></p>

<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA1U"><a href="./File:Radopholus_similis.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA1Y"><img resource="./File:Radopholus_similis.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Radopholus_similis.jpg/220px-Radopholus_similis.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="2901" data-file-height="1933" data-file-type="bitmap" height="147" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Radopholus_similis.jpg/330px-Radopholus_similis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Radopholus_similis.jpg/440px-Radopholus_similis.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwA1c"/></a><figcaption id="mwA1g"><i id="mwA1k"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Radopholus_similis" title="Radopholus similis" id="mwA1o">Radopholus similis</a></i> inside banana root, causing nematode root rot</figcaption></figure>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="24" id="mwA1s"><h3 id="Insects">Insects</h3>

<p id="mwA1w">Among the main insect pests of banana cultivation are two beetles that cause substantial economic losses, the banana borer <i id="mwA10"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cosmopolites_sordidus" title="Cosmopolites sordidus" id="mwA14">Cosmopolites sordidus</a></i> and the banana stem weevil <i id="mwA18"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Odoiporus_longicollis" title="Odoiporus longicollis" id="mwA2A">Odoiporus longicollis</a></i>. Other significant pests include <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aphid" title="Aphid" id="mwA2E">aphids</a> and scarring beetles.<sup about="#mwt441" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Padmanaban_2018_79-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Padmanaban 2018"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Padmanaban_2018-79"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Padmanaban_2018-79" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 79;" id="mwA2I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA2M">[79]</span></a></sup></p>

<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA2Q"><a href="./File:Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA2U"><img resource="./File:Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg/220px-Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="508" data-file-type="bitmap" height="213" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg/330px-Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg/440px-Cosmopolites_sordidus.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwA2Y"/></a><figcaption id="mwA2c">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cosmopolites_sordidus" title="Cosmopolites sordidus" id="mwA2g">banana borer</a> is a destructive pest that tunnels inside the plant.<sup about="#mwt443" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Padmanaban_2018_79-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Padmanaban 2018"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Padmanaban_2018-79" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 79;" id="mwA2k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA2o">[79]</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="25" id="mwA2s"><h2 id="Diseases">Diseases</h2>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt444" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"List of banana and plantain diseases"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA2w"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt444" id="mwA20">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_banana_and_plantain_diseases" title="List of banana and plantain diseases">List of banana and plantain diseases</a></div>

<p id="mwA24">Although in no danger of outright extinction, bananas of the Cavendish group, which dominate the global market, are under threat. Its predecessor '<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gros_Michel" title="Gros Michel" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA28">Gros Michel</a>', discovered in the 1820s, was similarly dominant but had to be replaced after widespread infections of Panama Disease. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Monocropping" title="Monocropping" id="mwA3A">Monocropping</a> of Cavendish similarly leaves it susceptible to disease and so threatens both commercial cultivation and small-scale subsistence farming.<sup about="#mwt450" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-NS060613_80-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"NS060613"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-NS060613-80" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 80;" id="mwA3E"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3I">[80]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt451" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Mont03_81-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Mont03"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Mont03-81" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 81;" id="mwA3M"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3Q">[81]</span></a></sup> Within the data gathered from the genes of hundreds of bananas, the botanist Julie Sardos has found several wild banana ancestors currently unknown to scientists, whose genes could provide a means of defense against banana crop diseases.<sup about="#mwt455" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-82" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-82"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-82" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 82;" id="mwA3U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3Y">[82]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA3c">Some commentators have remarked that those variants which could replace what much of the world considers a "typical banana" are so different that most people would not consider them the same fruit, and blame the decline of the banana on <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mendelian_inheritance" title="Mendelian inheritance" id="mwA3g">monogenetic</a> cultivation driven by short-term commercial motives.<sup about="#mwt458" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-NZH_54-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"NZH"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-NZH-54" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 54;" id="mwA3k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA3o">[54]</span></a></sup> Overall, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fungal_banana_disease" title="Fungal banana disease" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA3s">fungal diseases</a> are disproportionately important to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Small_island_developing_states" title="Small island developing states" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA3w">small island developing states</a>.<sup about="#mwt462" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas-et-al-2020_83-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Thomas-et-al-2020"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Thomas-et-al-2020-83"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Thomas-et-al-2020-83" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 83;" id="mwA30"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA34">[83]</span></a></sup></p>

<section data-mw-section-id="26" id="mwA38"><h3 id="Panama_disease">Panama disease</h3>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA4A"><a href="./File:Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA4E"><img alt="A banana tree cut horizontally to show the fungus development in the interior of the tree" resource="./File:Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg/220px-Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540" data-file-type="bitmap" height="165" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg/330px-Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg/440px-Panama_disease_of_banana_-_vascular_decoloration_on_pseudostem.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwA4I"/></a><figcaption id="mwA4M">Panama disease <i id="mwA4Q"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fusarium" title="Fusarium" id="mwA4U">Fusarium</a></i> fungus climbing up through the banana stem </figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwA4Y"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Panama_disease" title="Panama disease" id="mwA4c">Panama disease</a> is caused by a <i id="mwA4g"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fusarium" title="Fusarium" id="mwA4k">Fusarium</a></i> soil <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fungus" title="Fungus" id="mwA4o">fungus</a>, which enters the plants through the roots and travels with water into the trunk and leaves, producing <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gel" title="Gel" id="mwA4s">gels</a> and gums that cut off the flow of water and nutrients, causing the plant to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Wilting" title="Wilting" id="mwA4w">wilt</a>, and exposing the rest of the plant to lethal amounts of sunlight. Prior to 1960, almost all commercial banana production centered on the Gros Michel cultivar, which was highly susceptible.<sup about="#mwt466" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Bark08_84-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Bark08"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Bark08-84" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 84;" id="mwA40"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA44">[84]</span></a></sup> Cavendish was chosen as the replacement for Gros Michel because, among resistant cultivars, it produces the highest quality <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fruit" title="Fruit" id="mwA48">fruit</a>. However, more care is required for shipping the Cavendish,<sup about="#mwt470" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-85" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-85"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-85" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 85;" id="mwA5A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5E">[85]</span></a></sup> and its quality compared to Gros Michel is debated.<sup about="#mwt474" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Lessard_86-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Lessard"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Lessard-86"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Lessard-86" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 86;" id="mwA5I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5M">[86]</span></a></sup></p>

<section data-mw-section-id="27" id="mwA5Q"><h4 id="Fusarium_wilt_TR4">Fusarium wilt TR4</h4>

<p id="mwA5U"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tropical_Race_4" title="Tropical Race 4" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA5Y">Fusarium wilt TR4</a>, a reinvigorated strain of Panama disease, was discovered in 1993. This virulent form of Fusarium wilt has destroyed Cavendish plantations in several southeast Asian countries and spread to Australia and India.<sup about="#mwt487" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-karp_87-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"karp"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-karp-87"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-karp-87" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 87;" id="mwA5c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5g">[87]</span></a></sup> As the soil-based fungi can easily be carried on boots, clothing, or tools, the wilt spread to the Americas despite years of preventive efforts.<sup about="#mwt488" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-karp_87-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"karp"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-karp-87" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 87;" id="mwA5k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5o">[87]</span></a></sup> Without genetic diversity, Cavendish is highly susceptible to TR4, and the disease endangers its commercial production worldwide.<sup about="#mwt489" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-IBS_88-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"IBS"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-IBS-88" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 88;" id="mwA5s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA5w">[88]</span></a></sup> The only known defense to TR4 is <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Plant_disease_resistance" title="Plant disease resistance" id="mwA50">genetic resistance</a>.<sup about="#mwt490" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-karp_87-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"karp"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-karp-87" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 87;" id="mwA54"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA58">[87]</span></a></sup> This is conferred either by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./RGA2" title="RGA2" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA6A">RGA2</a>, a gene isolated from a TR4-resistant <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Diploid" title="Diploid" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA6E">diploid</a> banana, or by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nematode" title="Nematode" id="mwA6I">nematode</a>-derived Ced9.<sup about="#mwt491" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Dale-et-al-2017_89-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Dale-et-al-2017"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Dale-et-al-2017-89" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 89;" id="mwA6M"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6Q">[89]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt492" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ISAAA-Dale-2021_90-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ISAAA-Dale-2021"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-ISAAA-Dale-2021-90" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 90;" id="mwA6U"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6Y">[90]</span></a></sup> This may be achieved by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Genetic_modification" title="Genetic modification" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA6c">genetic modification</a>.<sup about="#mwt496" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Dale-et-al-2017_89-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Dale-et-al-2017"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Dale-et-al-2017-89"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Dale-et-al-2017-89" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 89;" id="mwA6g"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6k">[89]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt500" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-ISAAA-Dale-2021_90-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ISAAA-Dale-2021"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-ISAAA-Dale-2021-90"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-ISAAA-Dale-2021-90" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 90;" id="mwA6o"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA6s">[90]</span></a></sup> Experts state the need to enrich banana <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity" id="mwA6w">biodiversity</a> by producing diverse new banana varieties, not just having a focus on the Cavendish.<sup about="#mwt501" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-karp_87-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"karp"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-karp-87" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 87;" id="mwA60"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA64">[87]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="28" id="mwA68"><h3 id="Black_sigatoka">Black sigatoka</h3>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA7A"><a href="./File:Black_Sigatoka_(detail).jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA7E"><img resource="./File:Black_Sigatoka_(detail).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Black_Sigatoka_%28detail%29.jpg/220px-Black_Sigatoka_%28detail%29.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="976" data-file-type="bitmap" height="140" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Black_Sigatoka_%28detail%29.jpg/330px-Black_Sigatoka_%28detail%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Black_Sigatoka_%28detail%29.jpg/440px-Black_Sigatoka_%28detail%29.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwA7I"/></a><figcaption id="mwA7M">Leaf infected with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Black_sigatoka" title="Black sigatoka" id="mwA7Q">black sigatoka</a> </figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwA7U"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Black_sigatoka" title="Black sigatoka" id="mwA7Y">Black sigatoka</a> is a fungal leaf spot disease first observed in Fiji in 1963 or 1964. It is caused by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ascomycete" title="Ascomycete" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA7c">ascomycete</a> <i id="mwA7g">Mycosphaerella fijiensis</i>. The disease, also called black leaf streak, has spread to banana plantations throughout the tropics from infected banana leaves used as packing material. It affects all main cultivars of bananas and plantains (including the Cavendish cultivars<sup about="#mwt506" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Holmes_91-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Holmes"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Holmes-91" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 91;" id="mwA7k"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA7o">[91]</span></a></sup>), impeding <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis" id="mwA7s">photosynthesis</a> by blackening parts of the leaves, eventually killing the entire leaf. Starved for energy, fruit production falls by 50% or more, and the bananas that do grow <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ripening" title="Ripening" id="mwA7w">ripen</a> prematurely, making them unsuitable for export. The fungus has shown ever-increasing resistance to treatment, with the current expense for treating <span about="#mwt505" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"1"},"2":{"wt":"ha"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwA70">1 hectare (2.5 acres)</span> exceeding US$1,000 per year; spraying with fungicides may be required as often as 50 times a year. In addition to the expense, there is the question of how long intensive spraying can be environmentally justified.<sup about="#mwt510" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-92" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-92"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-92" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 92;" id="mwA74"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA78">[92]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt514" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-JGI_93-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"JGI"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-JGI-93"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-JGI-93" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 93;" id="mwA8A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA8E">[93]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="29" id="mwA8I"><h3 id="Banana_bunchy_top_virus">Banana bunchy top virus</h3>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA8M"><a href="./File:Banana_aphid_colony.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA8Q"><img alt="Infected Banana Plant" resource="./File:Banana_aphid_colony.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Banana_aphid_colony.jpg/220px-Banana_aphid_colony.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" data-file-type="bitmap" height="165" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Banana_aphid_colony.jpg/330px-Banana_aphid_colony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Banana_aphid_colony.jpg/440px-Banana_aphid_colony.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwA8U"/></a><figcaption id="mwA8Y">Colony of banana aphids (<i id="mwA8c"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pentalonia_nigronervosa" title="Pentalonia nigronervosa" id="mwA8g">Pentalonia nigronervosa</a></i>), <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Disease_vector" title="Disease vector" id="mwA8k">vector</a> of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_bunchy_top_virus" title="Banana bunchy top virus" id="mwA8o">banana bunchy top virus</a> </figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwA8s"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_bunchy_top_virus" title="Banana bunchy top virus" id="mwA8w">Banana bunchy top virus</a> (BBTV) is a plant virus of the genus <i id="mwA80">Babuvirus</i>, family <i id="mwA84">Nanonviridae</i> affecting <i id="mwA88">Musa</i> spp. (including banana, abaca, plantain and ornamental bananas) and <i id="mwA9A">Ensete</i> spp. in the family <i id="mwA9E">Musaceae</i>.<sup about="#mwt520" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-94" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-94"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-94" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 94;" id="mwA9I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9M">[94]</span></a></sup> Banana bunchy top disease (BBTD) symptoms include dark green streaks of variable length in leaf veins, midribs and petioles. Leaves become short and stunted as the disease progresses, becoming 'bunched' at the apex of the plant. Infected plants may produce no fruit or the fruit bunch may not emerge from the pseudostem.<sup about="#mwt522" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-techguide_95-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"techguide"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-techguide-95"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-techguide-95" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 95;" id="mwA9Q"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9U">[95]</span></a></sup> The virus is transmitted by the banana aphid <i id="mwA9Y"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pentalonia_nigronervosa" title="Pentalonia nigronervosa" id="mwA9c">Pentalonia nigronervosa</a></i> and is widespread in SE Asia, Asia, the Philippines, Taiwan, Oceania and parts of Africa. There is no cure for BBTD, but it can be effectively controlled by the eradication of diseased plants and the use of virus-free planting material.<sup about="#mwt526" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-96" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-96"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-96" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 96;" id="mwA9g"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9k">[96]</span></a></sup> No resistant cultivars have been found, but varietal differences in susceptibility have been reported. The commercially important Cavendish subgroup is severely affected.<sup about="#mwt527" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-techguide_95-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"techguide"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-techguide-95" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 95;" id="mwA9o"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA9s">[95]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="30" id="mwA9w"><h3 id="Banana_bacterial_wilt">Banana bacterial wilt</h3>

<p id="mwA90"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_Xanthomonas_wilt" title="Banana Xanthomonas wilt" id="mwA94">Banana bacterial wilt</a> (BBW) is a bacterial disease caused by <i id="mwA98"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Xanthomonas_campestris" title="Xanthomonas campestris" id="mwA-A">Xanthomonas campestris</a></i> pv. <i id="mwA-E">musacearum</i>.<sup about="#mwt531" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Tush04_97-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Tush04"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Tush04-97" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 97;" id="mwA-I"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-M">[97]</span></a></sup> First identified on a close relative of bananas, <i id="mwA-Q"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ensete_ventricosum" title="Ensete ventricosum" id="mwA-U">Ensete ventricosum</a></i>, in Ethiopia in the 1960s,<sup about="#mwt532" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Brad68_98-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Brad68"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Brad68-98" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 98;" id="mwA-Y"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-c">[98]</span></a></sup> BBW occurred in Uganda in 2001 affecting all banana cultivars. Since then BBW has been diagnosed in Central and East Africa including the banana growing regions of Rwanda, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, Tanzania, Kenya, Burundi, and Uganda.<sup about="#mwt533" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Mwan07_99-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Mwan07"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Mwan07-99" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 99;" id="mwA-g"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA-k">[99]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="31" id="mwA-o"><h2 id="Conservation_of_genetic_diversity">Conservation of genetic diversity</h2>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwA-s"><a href="./File:ITC_cold_room.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwA-w"><img resource="./File:ITC_cold_room.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ITC_cold_room.jpg/220px-ITC_cold_room.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="5067" data-file-height="3426" data-file-type="bitmap" height="149" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ITC_cold_room.jpg/330px-ITC_cold_room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ITC_cold_room.jpg/440px-ITC_cold_room.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwA-0"/></a><figcaption id="mwA-4">The cold storage room for the banana collection at <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bioversity_International" title="Bioversity International" id="mwA-8">Bioversity International</a>'s Musa Germplasm Transit Centre</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwA_A">Given the narrow range of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Genetic_diversity" title="Genetic diversity" id="mwA_E">genetic diversity</a> present in bananas and the many threats via <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Biotic_component" title="Biotic component" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA_I">biotic</a> (pests and diseases) and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Abiotic_component" title="Abiotic component" id="mwA_M">abiotic</a> threats (such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Drought" title="Drought" id="mwA_Q">drought</a>) stress, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology" id="mwA_U">conservation</a> of the full spectrum of banana <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Plant_genetic_resources" title="Plant genetic resources" id="mwA_Y">genetic resources</a> is ongoing.<sup about="#mwt539" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-genebank_100-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"genebank"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-genebank-100"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-genebank-100" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 100;" id="mwA_c"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_g">[100]</span></a></sup> In 2024, the economist Pascal Liu of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization" id="mwA_k">FAO</a> described the impact of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Global_warming" title="Global warming" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA_o">global warming</a> as an "enormous threat" to the world supply of bananas.<sup about="#mwt543" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-McGrath_2014_101-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"McGrath 2014"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-McGrath_2014-101"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-McGrath_2014-101" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 101;" id="mwA_s"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwA_w">[101]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwA_0">Banana <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Germplasm" title="Germplasm" id="mwA_4">germplasm</a> is conserved in many national and regional <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gene_banks" title="Gene banks" class="mw-redirect" id="mwA_8">gene banks</a>, and at the world's largest banana collection, the International <i id="mwBAA">Musa</i> Germplasm Transit Centre, managed by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bioversity_International" title="Bioversity International" id="mwBAE">Bioversity International</a> and hosted at <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./KU_Leuven" title="KU Leuven" id="mwBAI">KU Leuven</a> in Belgium.<sup about="#mwt549" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-musagermplasm_102-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"musagermplasm"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-musagermplasm-102"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-musagermplasm-102" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 102;" id="mwBAM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBAQ">[102]</span></a></sup> <i id="mwBAU">Musa</i> cultivars are usually seedless, and options for their long-term conservation are constrained by the vegetative nature of the plant's reproductive system. Consequently, they are conserved by three main methods: <i id="mwBAY"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./In_vivo" title="In vivo" id="mwBAc">in vivo</a></i> (planted in field collections), <i id="mwBAg"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./In_vitro" title="In vitro" id="mwBAk">in vitro</a></i> (as plantlets in test tubes within a controlled environment), and by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cryopreservation" title="Cryopreservation" id="mwBAo">cryopreservation</a> (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Meristem" title="Meristem" id="mwBAs">meristems</a> conserved in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Liquid_nitrogen" title="Liquid nitrogen" id="mwBAw">liquid nitrogen</a> at −196<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mwBA0"> </span>°C).<sup about="#mwt550" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-genebank_100-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"genebank"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-genebank-100" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 100;" id="mwBA4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBA8">[100]</span></a></sup></p> 

<p id="mwBBA">Genes from wild banana species are conserved as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./DNA" title="DNA" id="mwBBE">DNA</a> and as cryopreserved <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pollen" title="Pollen" id="mwBBI">pollen</a><sup about="#mwt553" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-genebank_100-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"genebank"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-genebank-100" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 100;" id="mwBBM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBBQ">[100]</span></a></sup> and banana seeds from wild species are also conserved, although less commonly, as they are difficult to regenerate. In addition, bananas and their <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crop_wild_relatives" title="Crop wild relatives" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBBU">crop wild relatives</a> are conserved <i id="mwBBY"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./In_situ" title="In situ" id="mwBBc">in situ</a></i> (in wild natural habitats where they evolved and continue to do so). Diversity is also conserved in farmers' fields where continuous cultivation, adaptation and improvement of cultivars is often carried out by small-scale farmers growing traditional local cultivars.<sup about="#mwt557" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-103" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-103"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-103" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 103;" id="mwBBg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBBk">[103]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="32" id="mwBBo"><h2 id="Nutrition">Nutrition</h2>
