</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><hr/><div class="wrap" style="padding:0.3em;line-height:1.2em;"><a rel="mw:ExtLink nofollow" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160101232525/http://ndb.nal.usda.gov/ndb/search/list?qlookup=09040&amp;format=Full" class="external text">Link to USDA Database entry</a>
 values are for edible portion</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below wrap" style="background:#e0e0e0;padding:0.3em;line-height:1.5em;font-weight:normal;"><sup>†</sup>Percentages estimated using <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Reference_Daily_Intake#Daily_Values" title="Reference Daily Intake">US<span typeof="mw:Entity"> </span>recommendations</a> for adults,<sup about="#mwt580" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FDADailyValues_104-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"FDADailyValues"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-FDADailyValues-104"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-FDADailyValues-104" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 104;" id="mwBB0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBB4">[104]</span></a></sup> except for potassium, which is estimated based on expert recommendation from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./National_Academies_of_Sciences,_Engineering,_and_Medicine" title="National Academies of Sciences, Engineering, and Medicine">the National Academies</a>.<sup about="#mwt585" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-NationalAcademiesPotassium_105-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"NationalAcademiesPotassium"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-NationalAcademiesPotassium-105"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-NationalAcademiesPotassium-105" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 105;" id="mwBB8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBCA">[105]</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p id="mwBCE">A raw banana (not including the peel) is 75% water, 23% <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate" id="mwBCI">carbohydrates</a>, 1% <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Protein_(nutrient)" title="Protein (nutrient)" id="mwBCM">protein</a>, and contains negligible <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fat" title="Fat" id="mwBCQ">fat</a>. A reference amount of <span about="#mwt588" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"100"},"2":{"wt":"g"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBCU">100 grams (3.5</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt588"> </span><span about="#mwt588">oz)</span> supplies 89 <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Calorie" title="Calorie" id="mwBCY">calories</a>, 31% of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Daily_Value" title="Daily Value" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBCc">Daily Value</a> of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vitamin_B6" title="Vitamin B6" id="mwBCg">vitamin B<sub id="mwBCk">6</sub></a>, and moderate amounts of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C" id="mwBCo">vitamin C</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Manganese_in_biology" title="Manganese in biology" id="mwBCs">manganese</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Potassium_in_biology" title="Potassium in biology" id="mwBCw">potassium</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dietary_fiber" title="Dietary fiber" id="mwBC0">dietary fiber</a>, with no other <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Micronutrient" title="Micronutrient" id="mwBC4">micronutrients</a> in significant content (table).</p>

<p id="mwBC8">Although bananas are commonly thought to contain exceptional potassium content,<sup about="#mwt596" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-edwards_106-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"edwards"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-edwards-106"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-edwards-106" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 106;" id="mwBDA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDE">[106]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt600" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-107" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-107"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-107" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 107;" id="mwBDI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDM">[107]</span></a></sup> their actual potassium content is not high per typical food serving, having only 12% of the Daily Value for potassium (considered a moderate level of the DV; table). The potassium-content ranking for bananas among fruits, vegetables, legumes, and many other foods is relatively medium.<sup about="#mwt604" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-rank_108-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"rank"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-rank-108"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-rank-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwBDQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDU">[108]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt608" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-eatright_109-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"eatright"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-eatright-109"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-eatright-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwBDY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDc">[109]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBDg">Individuals with a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Latex_allergy" title="Latex allergy" id="mwBDk">latex allergy</a> may experience a reaction to bananas.<sup about="#mwt610" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Tayl04_110-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Tayl04"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Tayl04-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwBDo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBDs">[110]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="33" id="mwBDw"><h2 id="Uses">Uses</h2>

<section data-mw-section-id="34" id="mwBD0"><h3 id="Culinary">Culinary</h3>

<section data-mw-section-id="35" id="mwBD4"><h4 id="Fruit">Fruit</h4>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt611" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Cooking plantain"},"2":{"wt":"List of banana dishes"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBD8"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt611" id="mwBEA">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cooking_plantain" title="Cooking plantain" class="mw-redirect">Cooking plantain</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_banana_dishes" title="List of banana dishes">List of banana dishes</a></div>

<p id="mwBEE">Bananas are a staple <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Starch" title="Starch" id="mwBEI">starch</a> for many tropical populations. Depending upon cultivar and ripeness, the flesh can vary in taste from starchy to sweet, and texture from firm to mushy. Both the skin and inner part can be eaten raw or cooked. The primary component of the aroma of fresh bananas is <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Isoamyl_acetate" title="Isoamyl acetate" id="mwBEM">isoamyl acetate</a> (also known as <i id="mwBEQ">banana oil</i>), which, along with several other compounds such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Butyl_acetate" title="Butyl acetate" id="mwBEU">butyl acetate</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Isobutyl_acetate" title="Isobutyl acetate" id="mwBEY">isobutyl acetate</a>, is a significant contributor to banana flavor.<sup about="#mwt615" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Mui02_111-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Mui02"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Mui02-111" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 111;" id="mwBEc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBEg">[111]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBEk">Plantains are eaten cooked, such as made into fritters.<sup about="#mwt625" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-112" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-112"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-112" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 112;" id="mwBEo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBEs">[112]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pisang_goreng" title="Pisang goreng" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBEw">Pisang goreng</a>, bananas fried with batter is a popular street food in Southeast Asia.<sup about="#mwt629" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Street_Food_113-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Street Food"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Street_Food-113"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Street_Food-113" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 113;" id="mwBE0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBE4">[113]</span></a></sup> Bananas feature in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Philippine_cuisine" title="Philippine cuisine" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBE8">Philippine cuisine</a>, with desserts like <i id="mwBFA"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Maruya_(Filipino_cuisine)" title="Maruya (Filipino cuisine)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBFE">maruya</a></i> banana fritters.<sup about="#mwt633" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-114" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-114"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-114" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 114;" id="mwBFI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFM">[114]</span></a></sup> Bananas can be made into fruit preserves.<sup about="#mwt637" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-115" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-115"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-115" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 115;" id="mwBFQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFU">[115]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_chips" title="Banana chips" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBFY">Banana chips</a> are a snack produced from sliced and fried bananas, such as in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Kerala" title="Kerala" id="mwBFc">Kerala</a>.<sup about="#mwt638" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Hindu130413_116-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Hindu130413"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Hindu130413-116" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 116;" id="mwBFg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFk">[116]</span></a></sup> Dried bananas are ground to make <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_flour" title="Banana flour" id="mwBFo">banana flour</a>.<sup about="#mwt642" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-business-goes-bananas_117-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"business-goes-bananas"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-business-goes-bananas-117"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-business-goes-bananas-117" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 117;" id="mwBFs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBFw">[117]</span></a></sup></p> 

<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" typeof="mw:Extension/gallery" about="#mwt644" data-mw='{"name":"gallery","attrs":{"mode":"packed","heights":"150"},"body":{}}' id="mwBF0">

</section><section data-mw-section-id="36" id="mwBHU"><h4 id="Flowers">Flowers</h4>

<p id="mwBHY">Banana flowers (also called "banana hearts" or "banana blossoms") are used as a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vegetable" title="Vegetable" id="mwBHc">vegetable</a><sup about="#mwt650" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-118" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-118"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-118" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 118;" id="mwBHg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBHk">[118]</span></a></sup> in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./South_Asian_cuisine" title="South Asian cuisine" id="mwBHo">South Asian</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Southeast_Asian_cuisine" title="Southeast Asian cuisine" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBHs">Southeast Asian cuisine</a>. The flavor resembles that of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Artichoke" title="Artichoke" id="mwBHw">artichoke</a>. As with artichokes, both the fleshy part of the bracts and the heart are edible.<sup about="#mwt654" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-119" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-119"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-119" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 119;" id="mwBH0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBH4">[119]</span></a></sup></p>

<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" typeof="mw:Extension/gallery" about="#mwt656" data-mw='{"name":"gallery","attrs":{"mode":"packed","heights":"150"},"body":{}}' id="mwBH8">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 226px;" id="mwBIA"><div class="thumb" style="width: 224px;" id="mwBIE"><span typeof="mw:File" id="mwBII"><a href="./File:Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Banana flowers and leaves on sale in Thailand" id="mwBIM"><img alt="Banana flowers and leaves on sale in Thailand" resource="./File:Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg/336px-Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" data-file-type="bitmap" height="150" width="224" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg/505px-Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg/672px-Thanin_market_banana_flowers_and_leaves.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBIQ"/></a></span></div><div class="gallerytext" id="mwBIU">Banana flowers and leaves on sale in Thailand</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202px;" id="mwBIY"><div class="thumb" style="width: 200px;" id="mwBIc"><span typeof="mw:File" id="mwBIg"><a href="./File:Bananajf.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Kilawin na pusô ng saging, a Filipino dish of banana flowers" id="mwBIk"><img alt="Kilawin na pusô ng saging, a Filipino dish of banana flowers" resource="./File:Bananajf.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bananajf.jpg/300px-Bananajf.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" data-file-type="bitmap" height="150" width="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bananajf.jpg/451px-Bananajf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Bananajf.jpg/600px-Bananajf.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBIo"/></a></span></div><div class="gallerytext" id="mwBIs"><i id="mwBIw">Kilawin na pusô ng saging</i>, a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cuisine_of_the_Philippines" title="Cuisine of the Philippines" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBI0">Filipino dish</a> of banana flowers</div></li>
</ul>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="37" id="mwBI4"><h4 id="Leaf">Leaf</h4>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt657" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Banana leaf"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBI8"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt657" id="mwBJA">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_leaf" title="Banana leaf">Banana leaf</a></div>

<p id="mwBJE">Banana leaves are large, flexible, and waterproof. While generally too tough to actually be eaten, they are often used as ecologically friendly disposable food containers or as "plates" in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./South_Asia" title="South Asia" id="mwBJI">South Asia</a> and several <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia" id="mwBJM">Southeast Asian</a> countries.<sup about="#mwt665" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-120" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-120"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-120" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 120;" id="mwBJQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJU">[120]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Indonesian_cuisine" title="Indonesian cuisine" id="mwBJY">Indonesian cuisine</a>, banana leaf is employed in cooking methods like <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pepes" title="Pepes" id="mwBJc">pepes</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Botok" title="Botok" id="mwBJg">botok</a>; banana leaf packages containing food ingredients and spices are cooked in steam or in boiled water, or are grilled on charcoal. Certain types of tamales are wrapped in banana leaves instead of corn husks.<sup about="#mwt669" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-121" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-121"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-121" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 121;" id="mwBJk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJo">[121]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBJs">When used so for steaming or grilling, the banana leaves protect the food ingredients from burning and add a subtle sweet flavor.<sup about="#mwt673" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-morton_1-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"morton"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-morton-1" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 1;" id="mwBJw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJ0">[1]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./South_India" title="South India" id="mwBJ4">South India</a>, it is customary to serve traditional food on a banana leaf.<sup about="#mwt677" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-122" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-122"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-122" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 122;" id="mwBJ8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBKA">[122]</span></a></sup> In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu" id="mwBKE">Tamil Nadu</a> (India), dried banana leaves are used as to pack food and to make cups to hold liquid food items.<sup about="#mwt681" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Kora_2019_123-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Kora 2019"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Kora_2019-123"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Kora_2019-123" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 123;" id="mwBKI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBKM">[123]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" typeof="mw:Extension/gallery" about="#mwt683" data-mw='{"name":"gallery","attrs":{"mode":"packed","heights":"150px"},"body":{}}' id="mwBKQ">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202px;" id="mwBKU"><div class="thumb" style="width: 200px;" id="mwBKY"><span typeof="mw:File" id="mwBKc"><a href="./File:Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Banana leaf as disposable plate for chicken satay in Java" id="mwBKg"><img alt="Banana leaf as disposable plate for chicken satay in Java" resource="./File:Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg/300px-Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1984" data-file-height="1488" data-file-type="bitmap" height="150" width="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg/451px-Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg/600px-Chicken_satay_on_banana_leaf_in_Java.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBKk"/></a></span></div><div class="gallerytext" id="mwBKo">Banana leaf as disposable plate for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chicken_satay" title="Chicken satay" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBKs">chicken satay</a> in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Java" title="Java" id="mwBKw">Java</a></div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202px;" id="mwBK0"><div class="thumb" style="width: 200px;" id="mwBK4"><span typeof="mw:File" id="mwBK8"><a href="./File:Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Nicaraguan Nacatamales, in banana leaves, ready to be steamed" id="mwBLA"><img alt="Nicaraguan Nacatamales, in banana leaves, ready to be steamed" resource="./File:Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg/300px-Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="432" data-file-type="bitmap" height="150" width="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg/451px-Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/03/Nacatamales_in_steamer.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBLE"/></a></span></div><div class="gallerytext" id="mwBLI">Nicaraguan <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nacatamal" title="Nacatamal" id="mwBLM">Nacatamales</a>, in banana leaves, ready to be steamed</div></li>
</ul>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="38" id="mwBLQ"><h4 id="Trunk">Trunk</h4>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt684" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Banana pith"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBLU"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt684" id="mwBLY">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_pith" title="Banana pith">Banana pith</a></div>

<p id="mwBLc">The tender core of the banana plant's trunk is also used in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./South_Asian_cuisine" title="South Asian cuisine" id="mwBLg">South Asian</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Southeast_Asian_cuisine" title="Southeast Asian cuisine" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBLk">Southeast Asian cuisine</a>. Examples include the Burmese dish <i id="mwBLo"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mohinga" title="Mohinga" id="mwBLs">mohinga</a></i>, and the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Filipino_cuisine" title="Filipino cuisine" id="mwBLw">Filipino</a> dishes <i id="mwBL0"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Inubaran" title="Inubaran" id="mwBL4">inubaran</a></i> and <i id="mwBL8"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Kadyos,_manok,_kag_ubad" title="Kadyos, manok, kag ubad" id="mwBMA">kadyos, manok, kag ubad</a></i>.<sup about="#mwt692" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Polistico_124-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Polistico"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Polistico-124"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Polistico-124" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 124;" id="mwBME"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMI">[124]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt696" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Polistico2_125-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Polistico2"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Polistico2-125"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Polistico2-125" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 125;" id="mwBMM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMQ">[125]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" typeof="mw:Extension/gallery" about="#mwt698" data-mw='{"name":"gallery","attrs":{"mode":"packed","heights":"150px"},"body":{}}' id="mwBMU">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 152px;" id="mwBMY"><div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;" id="mwBMc"><span typeof="mw:File" id="mwBMg"><a href="./File:Kaeng_yuak.JPG" class="mw-file-description" title="Kaeng yuak, a northern Thai curry of the core of the banana plant" id="mwBMk"><img alt="Kaeng yuak, a northern Thai curry of the core of the banana plant" resource="./File:Kaeng_yuak.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kaeng_yuak.JPG/225px-Kaeng_yuak.JPG" decoding="async" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1918" data-file-type="bitmap" height="150" width="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kaeng_yuak.JPG/338px-Kaeng_yuak.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kaeng_yuak.JPG/450px-Kaeng_yuak.JPG 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBMo"/></a></span></div><div class="gallerytext" id="mwBMs"><i id="mwBMw">Kaeng yuak</i>, a northern <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Thai_curry" title="Thai curry" id="mwBM0">Thai curry</a> of the core of the banana plant</div></li>
</ul>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="39" id="mwBM4"><h3 id="Paper_and_textiles">Paper and textiles</h3>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt699" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"further","href":"./Template:Further"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Manila hemp"},"2":{"wt":"Banana paper"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBM8"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt699" id="mwBNA">Further information: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Manila_hemp" title="Manila hemp" class="mw-redirect">Manila hemp</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_paper" title="Banana paper">Banana paper</a></div>

<p id="mwBNE">Banana fiber harvested from the pseudostems and leaves has been used for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Textile" title="Textile" id="mwBNI">textiles</a> in Asia since at least the 13th century. Both fruit-bearing and fibrous banana species have been used.<sup about="#mwt708" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-126" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-126"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-126" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 126;" id="mwBNM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBNQ">[126]</span></a></sup> In the Japanese system <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Kijōka-bashōfu" title="Kijōka-bashōfu" id="mwBNU">Kijōka-bashōfu</a>, leaves and shoots are cut from the plant periodically to ensure softness. Harvested shoots are first boiled in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lye" title="Lye" id="mwBNY">lye</a> to prepare fibers for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Yarn" title="Yarn" id="mwBNc">yarn</a>-making. These banana shoots produce fibers of varying degrees of softness, yielding yarns and textiles with differing qualities for specific uses. For example, the outermost fibers of the shoots are the coarsest, and are suitable for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tablecloth" title="Tablecloth" id="mwBNg">tablecloths</a>, while the softest innermost fibers are desirable for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Kimono" title="Kimono" id="mwBNk">kimono</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hakama" title="Hakama" id="mwBNo">kamishimo</a>. This traditional Japanese cloth-making process requires many steps, all performed by hand.<sup about="#mwt712" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-127" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-127"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-127" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 127;" id="mwBNs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBNw">[127]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_paper" title="Banana paper" id="mwBN0">Banana paper</a> can be made either from the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bark_(botany)" title="Bark (botany)" id="mwBN4">bark</a> of the banana plant, mainly for artistic purposes, or from the fibers of the stem and non-usable fruits. The paper may be hand-made or industrially processed.<sup about="#mwt716" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-128" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-128"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-128" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 128;" id="mwBN8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBOA">[128]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" typeof="mw:Extension/gallery" about="#mwt718" data-mw='{"name":"gallery","attrs":{"mode":"packed","heights":"150px"},"body":{}}' id="mwBOE">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 208.66666666667px;" id="mwBOI"><div class="thumb" style="width: 206.66666666667px;" id="mwBOM"><span typeof="mw:File" id="mwBOQ"><a </ul>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="40" id="mwBPc"><h3 id="Other_uses">Other uses</h3>

<p id="mwBPg">The large leaves of bananas may also be used as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Umbrella" title="Umbrella" id="mwBPk">umbrellas</a>.<sup about="#mwt720" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-morton_1-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"morton"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-morton-1" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 1;" id="mwBPo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBPs">[1]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBPw"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_peel" title="Banana peel" id="mwBP0">Banana peel</a> may have capability to extract <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Heavy_metal_(chemistry)" title="Heavy metal (chemistry)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBP4">heavy metal</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Contamination" title="Contamination" id="mwBP8">contamination</a> from river water, similar to other <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Water_purification" title="Water purification" id="mwBQA">purification</a> materials.<sup about="#mwt726" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-129" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-129"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-129" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 129;" id="mwBQE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQI">[129]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt730" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-130" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-130"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-130" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 130;" id="mwBQM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQQ">[130]</span></a></sup>
Waste bananas can be used to feed <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Livestock" title="Livestock" id="mwBQU">livestock</a>.<sup about="#mwt735" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-131" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-131"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-131" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 131;" id="mwBQY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQc">[131]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBQg">As with all living things, potassium-containing bananas emit <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Radioactivity" title="Radioactivity" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBQk">radioactivity</a> at low levels occurring naturally from the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Potassium-40" title="Potassium-40" id="mwBQo">potassium-40</a> (K-40) isotope.<sup about="#mwt742" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-frame_132-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"frame"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-frame-132"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-frame-132" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 132;" id="mwBQs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQw">[132]</span></a></sup> The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_equivalent_dose" title="Banana equivalent dose" id="mwBQ0">banana equivalent dose</a> of radiation was developed in 1995 as a simple teaching-tool to educate the public about the natural, small amount of K-40 radiation occurring in everyone and in common foods.<sup about="#mwt746" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-bed_133-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"bed"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-bed-133"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-bed-133" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 133;" id="mwBQ4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQ8">[133]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt747" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-edwards_106-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"edwards"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-edwards-106" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 106;" id="mwBRA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBRE">[106]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="41" id="mwBRI"><h2 id="Cultural_roles">Cultural roles</h2>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBRM"><a href="./File:River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBRQ"><img resource="./File:River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg/220px-River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1592" data-file-height="998" data-file-type="bitmap" height="138" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg/330px-River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg/440px-River_Kaveri_worship_Tiruchirappalli.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBRU"/></a><figcaption id="mwBRY">Coconut, banana and banana leaves used while worshiping <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Kaveri_River" title="Kaveri River" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBRc">River Kaveri</a> at <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tiruchirappalli" title="Tiruchirappalli" id="mwBRg">Tiruchirappalli</a>, India</figcaption></figure>

<section data-mw-section-id="42" id="mwBRk"><h3 id="Arts">Arts</h3>

<p id="mwBRo">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Edo_period" title="Edo period" id="mwBRs">Edo period</a> poet <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Matsuo_Bashō" title="Matsuo Bashō" id="mwBRw">Matsuo Bashō</a> is named after the Japanese word 芭蕉 (<span title="Japanese-language text" about="#mwt749" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"lang","href":"./Template:Lang"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"ja"},"2":{"wt":"Bashō"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBR0"><i lang="ja">Bashō</i></span><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Articles_containing_Japanese-language_text" about="#mwt749" id="mwBR4"/>) for the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Musa_basjoo" title="Musa basjoo" id="mwBR8">Japanese banana</a>. The <span title="Japanese-language text" about="#mwt750" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"lang","href":"./Template:Lang"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"ja"},"2":{"wt":"Bashō"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBSA"><i lang="ja">Bashō</i></span><link rel="mw:PageProp/Category" href="./Category:Articles_containing_Japanese-language_text" about="#mwt750" id="mwBSE"/> planted in his garden by a grateful student became a source of inspiration to his poetry, as well as a symbol of his life and home.<sup about="#mwt754" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-134" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-134"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-134" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 134;" id="mwBSI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBSM">[134]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBSQ">The song "<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Yes!_We_Have_No_Bananas" title="Yes! We Have No Bananas" id="mwBSU">Yes! We Have No Bananas</a>" was written by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Frank_Silver" title="Frank Silver" id="mwBSY">Frank Silver</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Irving_Cohn" title="Irving Cohn" id="mwBSc">Irving Cohn</a> and originally released in 1923; for many decades, it was the best-selling <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sheet_music" title="Sheet music" id="mwBSg">sheet music</a> in history. Since then the song has been rerecorded several times and has been particularly popular during banana shortages.<sup about="#mwt760" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-shaw_135-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"shaw"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-shaw-135"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-shaw-135" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 135;" id="mwBSk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBSo">[135]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt764" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Koeppel_136-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Koeppel"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Koeppel-136"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-Koeppel-136" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 136;" id="mwBSs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBSw">[136]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBS0">A person slipping on a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Banana_peel" title="Banana peel" id="mwBS4">banana peel</a> has been a staple of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Physical_comedy" title="Physical comedy" id="mwBS8">physical comedy</a> for generations. An American comedy recording from 1910 features a popular character of the time, "Uncle Josh", claiming to describe his own such incident.<sup about="#mwt769" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-137" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-137"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-137" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 137;" id="mwBTA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBTE">[137]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBTI">The cover artwork for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./The_Velvet_Underground_&amp;_Nico" title="The Velvet Underground &amp; Nico" id="mwBTM">the debut album</a> of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./The_Velvet_Underground" title="The Velvet Underground" id="mwBTQ">The Velvet Underground</a> features a banana made by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol" id="mwBTU">Andy Warhol</a>. On the original vinyl LP version, the design allowed the listener to "peel" this banana to find a pink, peeled phallic banana on the inside.<sup about="#mwt774" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-demain_138-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"demain"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-demain-138"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-demain-138" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 138;" id="mwBTY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBTc">[138]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBTg">Italian artist <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Maurizio_Cattelan" title="Maurizio Cattelan" id="mwBTk">Maurizio Cattelan</a> created a concept art piece titled <i id="mwBTo">Comedian</i><sup about="#mwt780" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-139" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-139"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-139" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 139;" id="mwBTs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBTw">[139]</span></a></sup> involving taping a banana to a wall using silver duct tape. The piece was exhibited briefly at the Art Basel in Miami before being removed from the exhibition and eaten without permission in another artistic stunt titled <i id="mwBT0">Hungry Artist</i> by New York artist <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./David_Datuna" title="David Datuna" id="mwBT4">David Datuna</a>.<sup about="#mwt784" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-140" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-140"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-140" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 140;" id="mwBT8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBUA">[140]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="43" id="mwBUE"><h3 id="Religion_and_folklore">Religion and folklore</h3>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBUI"><a href="./File:XRF-Tani-.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBUM"><img resource="./File:XRF-Tani-.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/XRF-Tani-.jpg/170px-XRF-Tani-.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="588" data-file-height="828" data-file-type="bitmap" height="239" width="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/XRF-Tani-.jpg/255px-XRF-Tani-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/XRF-Tani-.jpg/340px-XRF-Tani-.jpg 2x" class="mw-file-element" id="mwBUQ"/></a><figcaption id="mwBUU"><i id="mwBUY"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nang_Tani" title="Nang Tani" id="mwBUc">Nang Tani</a></i>, the female <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ghost" title="Ghost" id="mwBUg">ghost</a> of Thai folklore that haunts banana plants</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwBUk">In India, bananas serve a prominent part in many festivals and occasions of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hindu" title="Hindu" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBUo">Hindus</a>. In South Indian weddings, particularly <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tamil_culture" title="Tamil culture" id="mwBUs">Tamil weddings</a>, banana trees are tied in pairs to form an <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Arch" title="Arch" id="mwBUw">arch</a> as a blessing to the couple for a long-lasting, useful life.<sup about="#mwt790" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-mirror_141-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"mirror"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-mirror-141"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-mirror-141" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 141;" id="mwBU0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBU4">[141]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt794" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-earth_142-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"earth"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-earth-142"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-earth-142" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 142;" id="mwBU8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBVA">[142]</span></a></sup></p> 

<p id="mwBVE">In Thailand, it is believed that <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Musa_balbisiana" title="Musa balbisiana" id="mwBVI">a certain type</a> of banana plant may be inhabited by a spirit, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nang_Tani" title="Nang Tani" id="mwBVM">Nang Tani</a>, a type of ghost related to trees and similar plants that manifests itself as a young woman.<sup about="#mwt800" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-143" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-143"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-143" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 143;" id="mwBVQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBVU">[143]</span></a></sup> Often people tie a length of colored satin cloth around the pseudostem of the banana plants.<sup about="#mwt804" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-144" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-144"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-144" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 144;" id="mwBVY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBVc">[144]</span></a></sup></p> 

<p id="mwBVg">In <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ethnic_Malays" title="Ethnic Malays" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBVk">Malay folklore</a>, the ghost known as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pontianak_(folklore)" title="Pontianak (folklore)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBVo">Pontianak</a> is associated with banana plants (<i id="mwBVs">pokok pisang</i>), and its spirit is said to reside in them during the day.<sup about="#mwt809" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-145" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-145"}}'><a href="./Banana#cite_note-145" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 145;" id="mwBVw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBV0">[145]</span></a></sup></p>
